# *Star Wars: The Mandalorian*

[Edit](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Mandalorian?veaction=edit) 

* [Edit source](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Mandalorian?action=edit)
* [History](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Mandalorian?action=history)
* [Purge](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Mandalorian?action=purge)
* [Talk (60)](/wiki/Talk:Star_Wars:_The_Mandalorian)

[![This article details a subject that is considered canon.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](/wiki/Canon "This article details a subject that is considered canon.")[![The subject of this article takes place in the New Republic era.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](/wiki/New_Republic_Era "The subject of this article takes place in the New Republic era.")[![The subject of this article exists in or is relevant to the real world.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](/wiki/Category:Real-world_media "The subject of this article exists in or is relevant to the real world.")

This article is about **the television series**. You may be looking for **the title character, [Din Djarin](/wiki/Din_Djarin "Din Djarin"), or the first episode of the series, subtitled "[The Mandalorian](/wiki/Chapter_1:_The_Mandalorian "Chapter 1: The Mandalorian")"**.

[![The-Mandalorian-logo](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/4/4f/The-Mandalorian-logo.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/500?cb=20210211153541)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/4/4f/The-Mandalorian-logo.png/revision/latest?cb=20210211153541 "The-Mandalorian-logo")

## *Star Wars: The Mandalorian*

## Production information

### Format

Live-action[[1]](#cite_note-New_Series-1)

### Episode count

24[[2]](#cite_note-Writers_Guild-2)

### No. of seasons

3

### Network(s)

[Disney+](/wiki/Disney%2B "Disney+")[[1]](#cite_note-New_Series-1)

### First aired

[November 12](/wiki/November_12 "November 12"), [2019](/wiki/2019 "2019")[[3]](#cite_note-Poster_Revealed-3)

## Chronological information

### Timeline

[9 ABY](/wiki/9_ABY "9 ABY")[[16]](#cite_note-Date-16)

[[Source]](https://starwars.fandom.com/wiki/Template:TelevisionSeries)

:   "*I'm trying to evoke the aesthetics of not just the original trilogy but the first film. Not just the first film but the first act of the first film. What was it like on Tatooine? What was going on in that cantina? That has fascinated me since I was a child, and I love the idea of the darker, freakier side of Star Wars, the Mad Max aspect of Star Wars.*"
:   ―Jon Favreau[[17]](#cite_note-Hollywood_Reporter-17)

***Star Wars: The Mandalorian***, alternatively titled as simply ***The Mandalorian***, is a live-action space western *[Star Wars](/wiki/Star_Wars "Star Wars")* television series developed by [Lucasfilm](/wiki/Lucasfilm "Lucasfilm"). The series takes place about five [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") after the events of the [1983](/wiki/1983 "1983") film [*Star Wars*: Episode VI *Return of the Jedi*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_VI_Return_of_the_Jedi "Star Wars: Episode VI Return of the Jedi") and about twenty-five years before the events of the [2015](/wiki/2015 "2015") film [*Star Wars*: Episode VII *The Force Awakens*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_VII_The_Force_Awakens "Star Wars: Episode VII The Force Awakens") and airs exclusively on Disney's streaming service, [Disney+](/wiki/Disney%2B "Disney+"), which launched on [November 12](/wiki/November_12 "November 12"), [2019](/wiki/2019 "2019"). [Jon Favreau](/wiki/Jon_Favreau "Jon Favreau") is the creator, writer, and executive producer of the series. Directors include [Dave Filoni](/wiki/Dave_Filoni "Dave Filoni"), [Deborah Chow](/wiki/Deborah_Chow "Deborah Chow"), [Rick Famuyiwa](/wiki/Rick_Famuyiwa "Rick Famuyiwa"), [Bryce Dallas Howard](/wiki/Bryce_Dallas_Howard "Bryce Dallas Howard"), and [Taika Waititi](/wiki/Taika_Waititi "Taika Waititi").

[Season One](/wiki/The_Mandalorian_Season_One "The Mandalorian Season One") episodes debuted on Fridays at 08:01 UTC (3:01 AM EST), with the exception of the first and seventh episodes of that season. After the first season's conclusion, an eight-episode behind the scenes series was released starting [May](/wiki/May "May") [2020](/wiki/2020 "2020"), titled *[Disney Gallery: The Mandalorian](/wiki/Disney_Gallery:_The_Mandalorian "Disney Gallery: The Mandalorian")*. On [October 30](/wiki/October_30 "October 30"), 2020, the [second season](/wiki/The_Mandalorian_Season_Two "The Mandalorian Season Two") premiered on Disney+. Season Two episodes debuted on Fridays at 08:01 UTC (3:01 AM EST). Two *Disney Gallery: The Mandalorian* specials about the making of the second season were released afterwards.

The series *[The Book of Boba Fett](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Book_of_Boba_Fett "Star Wars: The Book of Boba Fett")* premiered on [December 29](/wiki/December_29 "December 29"), [2021](/wiki/2021 "2021"), and featured several characters from the *The Mandalorian* after the events of the second season. The [third season](/wiki/The_Mandalorian_Season_Three "The Mandalorian Season Three") premiered on [March 1](/wiki/March_1 "March 1"), [2023](/wiki/2023 "2023"), and a [fourth season](/wiki/The_Mandalorian_Season_Four "The Mandalorian Season Four") is currently being written by Jon Favreau. An upcoming film spinoff titled *[The Mandalorian and Grogu](/wiki/The_Mandalorian_and_Grogu "The Mandalorian and Grogu")* will release on [May 22](/wiki/May_22 "May 22"), [2026](/wiki/2026 "2026") and the series' story will be concluded by an [upcoming untitled film](/wiki/Untitled_Star_Wars_film_(Dave_Filoni) "Untitled Star Wars film (Dave Filoni)") directed by Filoni.

## Official description[]

:   "*It's like after the Roman Empire falls, or when you don't have a centralized shogun in Japan—and, of course, the Old West, when there wasn't any government in the areas that had not yet been settled.*"
:   ―Jon Favreau[[18]](#cite_note-Unmasked-18)

*After the stories of Jango and Boba Fett, another warrior emerges in the* Star Wars *universe.* The Mandalorian *is set after the fall of the Empire and before the emergence of the First Order. We follow the travels of a lone gunfighter in the outer reaches of the galaxy far from the authority of the New Republic....*[[19]](#cite_note-The_Mandalorian_FB-19)

## Development[]

:   "*I had a pitch for a concept of following the archetypes that influenced George Lucas whether it was the Western, the samurai film, the World War II film, earlier space operas, cliffhangers, Flash Gordon—looking at the films and the archetypes that influenced George was a way for us to make a smaller story that would work for the scale of the small screen and get back to the basics.*"
:   ―Jon Favreau[[20]](#cite_note-WGA-20)

In [2005](/wiki/2005 "2005"),[[21]](#cite_note-Thank_the_Maker-21) [George Lucas](/wiki/George_Lucas "George Lucas") began developing a [live-action TV series](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Underworld "Star Wars: Underworld") that would explore the criminal underworld of *Star Wars*.[[22]](#cite_note-22) Producer [Rick McCallum](/wiki/Rick_McCallum "Rick McCallum") compared it to [*Deadwood*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deadwood_(TV_series) "wikipedia:Deadwood (TV series)") and [*The Godfather*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Godfather_(film_series) "wikipedia:The Godfather (film series)"),[[23]](#cite_note-23)[[24]](#cite_note-Prague-24) and hinted that it would involve bounty hunters.[[25]](#cite_note-Mccallum-25) At the [2007](/wiki/2007 "2007") [Toy Fair](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_International_Toy_Fair "wikipedia:American International Toy Fair"), a poster teased upcoming *Star Wars* projects, with the TV series represented by a picture of Boba Fett.[[26]](#cite_note-Temple_Archives-26) After 50 scripts were completed, Lucas and McCallum felt that the show would be too expensive to produce with the current technology, and thus decided to put the project on hold.[[27]](#cite_note-Live_Action_Update-27)[[24]](#cite_note-Prague-24) In [2012](/wiki/2012 "2012"), Lucas sold [Lucasfilm](/wiki/Lucasfilm "Lucasfilm") to [The Walt Disney Company](/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company "The Walt Disney Company").[[28]](#cite_note-Disney_Lucasfilm_PR-28) Under Disney, a [film centered on Boba Fett](/wiki/Untitled_Boba_Fett_film "Untitled Boba Fett film") was reportedly planned to be produced as part of its [*Anthology Series*](/wiki/Star_Wars_Anthology_Series "Star Wars Anthology Series").[[29]](#cite_note-EW_Boba-29)

In [September](/wiki/September "September") [2017](/wiki/2017 "2017"), Lucasfilm head [Kathleen Kennedy](/wiki/Kathleen_Kennedy "Kathleen Kennedy") reached out to [Jon Favreau](/wiki/Jon_Favreau "Jon Favreau") for possible ideas for [Disney+](/wiki/Disney%2B "Disney+"), for which the company looked to create original content. He expressed interest in doing something with the [Mandalorians](/wiki/Mandalorian "Mandalorian"), having reflected on some concepts he had developed when he first heard that Disney gained control of the franchise. In November, Favreau met with Kennedy and [Carrie Beck](/wiki/Carrie_Beck "Carrie Beck") to pitch his idea for the show. At the meeting, Kennedy told him that [Dave Filoni](/wiki/Dave_Filoni "Dave Filoni") was also interested in telling stories about Mandalorians. (Filoni had also talked with Kennedy about wanting to work in live-action; She then sent him visit the sets of some of the contemporary *Star Wars* films to study the productions.) Favreau was familiar with Filoni, having voiced the Mandalorian character [Pre Vizsla](/wiki/Pre_Vizsla "Pre Vizsla") on *[Star Wars: The Clone Wars](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars "Star Wars: The Clone Wars")*. A few days later, the three of them met again, this time accompanied by Filoni and [Christopher Yost](/wiki/Christopher_Yost "Christopher Yost").[[30]](#cite_note-Art_of_Mando-30) A new TV series was announced by Disney CEO [Robert Iger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Iger "wikipedia:Robert Iger") during a Disney quarterly earnings call on [November 9](/wiki/November_9 "November 9"), 2017.[[1]](#cite_note-New_Series-1)

On [May 10](/wiki/May_10 "May 10"), [2018](/wiki/2018 "2018"), in an interview with [Anthony Carboni](/wiki/Anthony_Carboni "Anthony Carboni") on the premier for *[Solo: A Star Wars Story](/wiki/Solo:_A_Star_Wars_Story "Solo: A Star Wars Story")*, Favreau revealed that he was halfway done with writing a season of the upcoming live-action *Star Wars* series.[[31]](#cite_note-Solo_premier-31) As producer Kennedy recalled: "I'd been talking to him, off and on, for a few years. He had this story, and suddenly the two of us realized, not only could this be told in the television space, but we could also push technology."[[32]](#cite_note-Abrams-32) During an interview with Dan Casey of [Nerdist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nerdist "wikipedia:Nerdist") at the premiere, Favreau confirmed the show would take place seven [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") after the [Battle of Yavin](/wiki/Battle_of_Yavin "Battle of Yavin") and feature all-new characters. Favreau also revealed that even before he had the job, he had written four scripts to show Lucasfilm what the show would be[[33]](#cite_note-Details-33) and to ensure that his vision made it to the screen.[[17]](#cite_note-Hollywood_Reporter-17) As writing continued, he had many discussions with co-executive producer Filoni, who would give him feedback based on his experience working directly with George Lucas on *The Clone Wars*. Filoni would make sketches of Favreau's ideas, which would be given to the department.[[20]](#cite_note-WGA-20) Reflecting on the writing process, Favreau told *GQ Middle East*, "One thing [George Lucas] said to me was, 'remember, Jon, the real audience for all stories and all myths is the kids that are coming of age', because he's really a [Joseph Campbell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Campbell "wikipedia:Joseph Campbell") adherent."[[34]](#cite_note-Fav_and_Lucas-34) He also made a conscious effort to appeal to all types of *Star Wars* fans, telling *Entertainment Weekly*: "Part of what's fun is to see if we could merge the worlds of the original trilogy, the prequels, the sequels, *The Clone Wars*, and what's been considered canon up to this point and what's been considered part of [Legends](/wiki/Star_Wars_Legends "Star Wars Legends")."[[35]](#cite_note-EW_Favreau-35)

 [![The Mandalorian character sketches by Dave Filoni](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a1/The_Mandalorian_DF_sketch.png/revision/latest?cb=20181213144655) [![The Mandalorian character sketches by Dave Filoni](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a1/The_Mandalorian_DF_sketch.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/200?cb=20181213144655)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a1/The_Mandalorian_DF_sketch.png/revision/latest?cb=20181213144655) 

*The Mandalorian* character sketches by Dave Filoni

 

On [August 6](/wiki/August_6 "August 6"), 2018, [*The New York Times*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_New_York_Times "wikipedia:The New York Times") reported that Favreau's *Star Wars* series, which would be produced for Disney's new streaming service, was expected to cost around $100 million for 10 episodes. In an email to *The New York Times*, Favreau stated that the service would allow for the opportunity to tell stories that go for several chapters.[[36]](#cite_note-NYT_August-36) On [October 26](/wiki/October_26 "October 26"), 2018, it was reported that the rumored Boba Fett film had been scrapped, with Lucasfilm instead focusing on *The Mandalorian*.[[37]](#cite_note-bobano-37) On [November 13](/wiki/November_13 "November 13"), 2018, [Pedro Pascal](/wiki/Pedro_Pascal "Pedro Pascal") was reported to be in negotiations to play the lead role in the series.[[38]](#cite_note-Negotiations-38) The [next day](/wiki/November_14 "November 14"), [Gina Carano](/wiki/Gina_Carano "Gina Carano") was announced to have joined the cast according to [*Variety*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variety "wikipedia:Variety").[[39]](#cite_note-Gina-39) On [November 30](/wiki/November_30 "November 30"), *Variety* again reported that [Nick Nolte](/wiki/Nick_Nolte "Nick Nolte") had been added to the show's cast.[[40]](#cite_note-Nolte-40) On [December 12](/wiki/December_12 "December 12"), Lucasfilm officially announced the cast, confirming the casting of Pascal, Carano, and Nolte, along with [Giancarlo Esposito](/wiki/Giancarlo_Esposito "Giancarlo Esposito"), [Emily Swallow](/wiki/Emily_Swallow "Emily Swallow"), [Carl Weathers](/wiki/Carl_Weathers "Carl Weathers"), [Omid Abtahi](/wiki/Omid_Abtahi "Omid Abtahi"), and [Werner Herzog](/wiki/Werner_Herzog "Werner Herzog").[[13]](#cite_note-Cast_announced-13)

### Production[]

The series is mostly filmed on soundstages in Los Angeles,[[41]](#cite_note-New_Tech-41) with occasional plate photography in various international locations.[[42]](#cite_note-Hollywood_Jon-42) At the suggestion of [Rob Bredow](/wiki/Rob_Bredow "Rob Bredow"),[[43]](#cite_note-Kennedy_Plan-43) it uses a new technology known as "Stagecraft,"[[44]](#cite_note-Stagecraft-44) with special effects that utilize a [video game](/wiki/Star_Wars_video_games "Star Wars video games") engine developed by [Epic Games](/wiki/Epic_Games "Epic Games").[[45]](#cite_note-Innovators-45)[[46]](#cite_note-Acc_Demo-46) ILM also opened a new London-based division, [ILM TV](/wiki/Industrial_Light_%26_Magic "Industrial Light & Magic"), to work on *The Mandalorian* and other projects.[[47]](#cite_note-ILM_TV-47)

Favreau described his role as showrunner: "It's a lot like being a chef. You write the menu, you staff up with people who are great at what they do, you oversee and help guide the people who are actually cooking the food, working the line, and then at the end, you plate." He compared his work on the series to that of [*Iron Man*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron_Man_(2008_film) "wikipedia:Iron Man (2008 film)") (in that the release of the former would mark the launch of Disney+, whereas the latter marked the launch of the [Marvel Cinematic Universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe "wikipedia:Marvel Cinematic Universe")), noting that he didn't feel much pressure on either project.[[17]](#cite_note-Hollywood_Reporter-17) Director Bryce Dallas Howard described the production process as highly collaborative, with all the directors sharing an office, and the producers always open to ideas from the directors.[[48]](#cite_note-Different-48) During production, Favreau shared photos on his [Instagram](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instagram "wikipedia:Instagram") account.[[49]](#cite_note-Favreau's_Photos-49) George Lucas visited the set during production as part of a birthday surprise for Favreau.[[50]](#cite_note-George's_There!-50) While filming at a studio in [Manhattan Beach, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manhattan_Beach,_California "wikipedia:Manhattan Beach, California"), equipment was stolen from the set, prompting a police investigation.[[51]](#cite_note-Police-51)[[52]](#cite_note-Hollywood_Theft-52)

 [![Dave Filoni and Jon Favreau with members of the 501st](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/e/ef/DisneyGallery-Connections-510st.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20211001172517) [![Dave Filoni and Jon Favreau with members of the 501st](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/e/ef/DisneyGallery-Connections-510st.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/220?cb=20211001172517)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/e/ef/DisneyGallery-Connections-510st.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20211001172517) 

Dave Filoni and Jon Favreau with members of the 501st

 

The [first season](/wiki/The_Mandalorian_Season_One "The Mandalorian Season One") wrapped filming in [February](/wiki/February "February") 2019.[[53]](#cite_note-Wrapped-53) Each episode of the season reportedly cost 15 million to make.[[54]](#cite_note-54) Robert Iger viewed each Season One episode multiple times to give notes and track the show's progress.[[55]](#cite_note-Bloomberg-55) Members of the Star Wars costuming fan organization the [501st Legion](/wiki/501st_Legion_(fan_organization) "501st Legion (fan organization)") also participated as extras since the producers did not have enough [stormtrooper](/wiki/Stormtrooper "Stormtrooper") costumes.[[56]](#cite_note-The_Mandalorian_panel-56)[[57]](#cite_note-501_Mando-57)

On [April 2](/wiki/April_2 "April 2"), 2019, a [second season](/wiki/The_Mandalorian_Season_Two "The Mandalorian Season Two") for *The Mandalorian* was reportedly ordered by Lucasfilm.[[58]](#cite_note-EW_S2-58) When interviewed by [Collider](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collider_(website) "wikipedia:Collider (website)") about his [live-action remake](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Lion_King_(2019_film) "wikipedia:The Lion King (2019 film)") of [*The Lion King*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Lion_King "wikipedia:The Lion King"), Favreau commented that he was writing the second season and that pre-production was underway.[[59]](#cite_note-Season_2_Writing-59) The second season wrapped filming in [March](/wiki/March "March") 2020.[[60]](#cite_note-Season_2_Wrapped-60)

On [April 21](/wiki/April_21 "April 21"), [2020](/wiki/2020 "2020"), *[Variety](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variety_(magazine) "wikipedia:Variety (magazine)")* announced that a [third season](/wiki/The_Mandalorian_Season_Three "The Mandalorian Season Three") for *The Mandalorian* was reportedly in the works by Lucasfilm.[[61]](#cite_note-Season_3-61) On [December 10](/wiki/December_10 "December 10"), 2020, Kathleen Kennedy teased that the "next chapter" of *The Mandalorian* would arrive on [Christmas](/wiki/December_24 "December 24") of [2021](/wiki/2021 "2021").[[62]](#cite_note-Tease-62) However, on [December 21](/wiki/December_21 "December 21"), 2020, Jon Favreau appeared on Good Morning America on the [ABC Television Network](/wiki/ABC_Television_Network "ABC Television Network"), and clarified that *[The Book of Boba Fett](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Book_of_Boba_Fett "Star Wars: The Book of Boba Fett")* is currently in production, and will be released in [December](/wiki/December "December") 2021, while the third season of *The Mandalorian* will go into production after the filming of *The Book of Boba Fett* is completed.[[63]](#cite_note-GMA_YouTube-63) A [StarWars.com](/wiki/StarWars.com "StarWars.com") post later that day reiterated this, and stated that *The Mandalorian* Season Three would go into production in 2021.[[64]](#cite_note-Book_of_Boba_Announcement-64) Filming began in September 2021[[65]](#cite_note-ChipAndCo-65) and wrapped in March [2022](/wiki/2022 "2022").[[66]](#cite_note-Filming_wrapped-66)

### Music[]

On [December 19](/wiki/December_19 "December 19"), 2018, [Ludwig Göransson](/wiki/Ludwig_G%C3%B6ransson "Ludwig Göransson") was announced to be composing the music for the show.[[15]](#cite_note-Composer-15) Göransson had previously composed the music for director [Ryan Coogler's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ryan_Coogler "wikipedia:Ryan Coogler") 2018 film [*Black Panther*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Panther_(film) "wikipedia:Black Panther (film)"); Favreau met him through Coogler, and discussed the project a year before production began on *The Mandalorian*. As Favreau told the *Los Angeles Times*, he wanted the music to be "a little grittier, a little edgier and a little more tech-oriented, something that felt half-tech, half-classic." Göransson took his initial inspiration from a nature hike, going for an "organic" sound that made heavy use of woodwinds, combined with [electronic instruments](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electronic_musical_instrument "wikipedia:Electronic musical instrument") and orchestral music.[[67]](#cite_note-Goransson-67) The first season's soundtrack was released in a limited 8-LP set, produced exclusively by mondoshop.com.[[68]](#cite_note-Soundtrack-68)

Göransson also wrote the music for the second season of the show[[69]](#cite_note-Hollywood_Goransson-69) [The soundtrack of the first four episodes of the second season](/wiki/The_Mandalorian:_Season_2_-_Vol._1_(Chapters_9-12)_(Original_Score) "The Mandalorian: Season 2 - Vol. 1 (Chapters 9-12) (Original Score)") was released digitally on [November 20](/wiki/November_20 "November 20"), 2020.[[70]](#cite_note-Amazon_Score-70) [The soundtrack of the last four episodes of the second season](/wiki/The_Mandalorian:_Season_2_-_Vol._2_(Chapters_13-16)_(Original_Score) "The Mandalorian: Season 2 - Vol. 2 (Chapters 13-16) (Original Score)") was released digitally on [December 18](/wiki/December_18 "December 18"), 2020.[[71]](#cite_note-Digital_December-71)

## Release and reception[]

Favreau, Filoni, and most of the cast hosted a panel at [Celebration Chicago](/wiki/Celebration_Chicago "Celebration Chicago") on [April 14](/wiki/April_14 "April 14"), 2019, where the first footage premiered exclusively to fans in attendance.[[72]](#cite_note-Celebration_panel-72) A few days later, the cast appeared on [*Good Morning America*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Good_Morning_America "wikipedia:Good Morning America").[[73]](#cite_note-73) On [August 23](/wiki/August_23 "August 23"), 2019, *The Mandalorian*'s first trailer was released at the [D23 Expo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D23_(Disney) "wikipedia:D23 (Disney)") in Anaheim at a panel consisting of Favreau, Filoni, and cast members Pascal, Carano, Weathers, Waititi, and [Ming-Na Wen](/wiki/Ming-Na_Wen "Ming-Na Wen").[[74]](#cite_note-D23-74) The show was the cover story for the September 2019 issue of *Entertainment Weekly*.[[18]](#cite_note-Unmasked-18) On [October 19](/wiki/October_19 "October 19"), as part of their press day for Disney+, Disney showcased 27 minutes of footage for members of the press.[[75]](#cite_note-75) A second and final trailer was released on [October 28](/wiki/October_28 "October 28"), 2019.[[76]](#cite_note-Mandalorian_Final_Trailer-76) The series debuted on [November 12](/wiki/November_12 "November 12"), [2019](/wiki/2019 "2019").[[3]](#cite_note-Poster_Revealed-3) On November 13, a premier was held at Hollywood's El Capitan Theater. Three episodes were screened at the event,[[77]](#cite_note-77) and the cast and crew participated in a Q&A livestream.[[78]](#cite_note-78)

Following the success of the first season, Disney CEO Bob Iger revealed on [February 4](/wiki/February_4 "February 4"), 2020 that the second season would premiere on Disney+ in October 2020.[[79]](#cite_note-Season_2_Premiere_Date-79) He also suggested that characters may be introduced to the show that will receive their own spin-offs.[[80]](#cite_note-80) According to [Alan Horn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Horn "wikipedia:Alan Horn"), the [CCO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chief_creative_officer "wikipedia:Chief creative officer") of The Walt Disney Company, if the series proves to be a success, there's the possibility of a film adaptation for either Disney+ or a theatrical release.[[81]](#cite_note-81) On [September 2](/wiki/September_2 "September 2"), 2020, it was announced that the second season for the show would be releasing on [October 30](/wiki/October_30 "October 30"), 2020.[[82]](#cite_note-S2_Release_Date-82) The show was featured in the October 2020 issue of *Entertainment Weekly*.[[83]](#cite_note-EW_Mando_S2-83)

The spinoff series *The Book of Boba Fett* premiered on [December 29](/wiki/December_29 "December 29"), 2021,[[84]](#cite_note-BOBF_Release_Date-84) and featured several characters that appeared in *The Mandalorian* after the events of the second season.[[85]](#cite_note-BOBF_Chapter_7-85)

The third season takes place after the events of *The Book of Boba Fett*.[[11]](#cite_note-S3_Press_Release-11) During *[Celebration Anaheim](/wiki/Celebration_Anaheim_(2022) "Celebration Anaheim (2022)")* in 2022, it was announced that the season will premiere in February [2023](/wiki/2023 "2023"), and an exclusive teaser was shown.[[86]](#cite_note-Showcase-86) It was also announced that [Rick Famuyiwa](/wiki/Rick_Famuyiwa "Rick Famuyiwa") will executive produce and direct in the third season.[[12]](#cite_note-Rick_EP-12) The release was later delayed to [March 1](/wiki/March_1 "March 1").[[87]](#cite_note-S3_release_date-87)

The series was one of the most-watched series of 2019.[[88]](#cite_note-Global_Demand-88) In [July](/wiki/July "July") 2020, the first season was nominated for 15 [Emmy Awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emmy_Award "wikipedia:Emmy Award"), including Outstanding Drama Series.[[89]](#cite_note-Emmy_Noms-89) That September, it ended up winning 7 of the nominations.[[90]](#cite_note-Emmy_Wins-90) In February 2021, the second season was nominated for a [Golden Globe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Globe_Awards "wikipedia:Golden Globe Awards") for "Best Television Series (Drama)".[[91]](#cite_note-globe-91) In July 2021, the second season was nominated for 24 Emmy awards.[[92]](#cite_note-SW-The_Mandalorian_Receives_24_Emmy_Award_Nominations-92) That September, it ended up winning 7 of the nominations.[[93]](#cite_note-SW-The_Mandalorian_Wins_Seven_Emmy_Awards-93)

### Home Video[]

On August 21, 2023, it was announced that the first two seasons of The Mandalorian would be available on 4K Blu-ray in steelbook packaging. Bonus features include original box art by Attila Szarka, concept art cards, and never-before-seen featurettes. It was scheduled to be released on December 12, 2023, though pre-orders would start on August 28.[[94]](#cite_note-SW-The_Mandalorian_Seasons_1_and_2_Blast_Onto_4K_Ultra_HD_and_Blu-ray-94)[[95]](#cite_note-PhysicalMedia-95)

## Adaptations and tie-in media[]

*The Mandalorian*'s merchandise line debuted as part of [Triple Force Friday](/wiki/Force_Friday "Force Friday"), which was held on [October 4](/wiki/October_4 "October 4"), 2019.[[96]](#cite_note-Triple_Force_Friday-96) *[Disney Gallery: The Mandalorian](/wiki/Disney_Gallery:_The_Mandalorian "Disney Gallery: The Mandalorian")*, a series which focuses on behind-the-scenes aspects of *The Mandalorian*, premiered on [May 4](/wiki/May_4 "May 4"), 2020.[[97]](#cite_note-Gallery-97) A [*Mandalorian* publishing program](/wiki/The_Mandalorian_publishing_program "The Mandalorian publishing program") began in fall 2020.[[98]](#cite_note-SW-The_Mandalorian_Publishing_Program_Revealed_-_Exclusive-98) On [September 21](/wiki/September_21 "September 21"), 2020, Lucasfilm announced the "Mando Mondays" marketing campaign, in which new *Mandalorian* merchandise would become available each Monday, beginning on October 26 through December 21.[[99]](#cite_note-Mando_Mondays-99) Elements from the show were incorporated into various [video games](/wiki/Star_Wars_video_games "Star Wars video games"), including *[Star Wars: Galaxy of Heroes](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Galaxy_of_Heroes "Star Wars: Galaxy of Heroes")*,[[100]](#cite_note-Galaxy_of_Heroes-100) *[Minecraft Star Wars](/wiki/Minecraft_Star_Wars "Minecraft Star Wars")*,[[101]](#cite_note-Minecraft-101) *[Fortnite](/wiki/Fortnite "Fortnite")*,[[102]](#cite_note-Fortnite-102) and *[The Sims 4](/wiki/The_Sims_4 "The Sims 4")*.[[103]](#cite_note-SimsMando-103) *[Star Wars: The Old Republic](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Old_Republic "Star Wars: The Old Republic")*, a video game part of the [*Star Wars* Legends](/wiki/Star_Wars_Legends "Star Wars Legends") continuity, was updated with a new player armor inspired by *The Mandalorian* in the game's [Cartel Market](/wiki/Cartel_Market "Cartel Market").[[104]](#cite_note-SWTOR-104)

[↑](#cite_ref-Date_16-0) *[Star Wars: Timelines](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Timelines "Star Wars: Timelines")* dates the events of "[Chapter 1: The Mandalorian](/wiki/Chapter_1:_The_Mandalorian "Chapter 1: The Mandalorian")" of [*The Mandalorian* Season One](/wiki/The_Mandalorian_Season_One "The Mandalorian Season One") to [9 ABY](/wiki/9_ABY "9 ABY"). In addition, [SWInsider](/wiki/Star_Wars_Insider "Star Wars Insider") "[A Certain Point of View](/wiki/A_Certain_Point_of_View_(department) "A Certain Point of View (department)")" — [*Star Wars Insider* 228](/wiki/Star_Wars_Insider_228 "Star Wars Insider 228") also dates "[Part Seven: Dreams and Madness](/wiki/Part_Seven:_Dreams_and_Madness "Part Seven: Dreams and Madness")" to nine [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") after the events of [*Star Wars*: Episode IV *A New Hope*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_IV_A_New_Hope "Star Wars: Episode IV A New Hope"), which corresponds to 9 [ABY](/wiki/%27ABY-BBY%27_dating_system "'ABY-BBY' dating system") per *Timelines*. "Part Seven: Dreams and Madness" takes place after the [liberation of Mandalore](/wiki/Liberation_of_Mandalore "Liberation of Mandalore"), which is the main event depicted in "[Chapter 23: The Spies](/wiki/Chapter_23:_The_Spies "Chapter 23: The Spies")" and "[Chapter 24: The Return](/wiki/Chapter_24:_The_Return "Chapter 24: The Return")," the final two episodes of [*The Mandalorian* Season Three](/wiki/The_Mandalorian_Season_Three "The Mandalorian Season Three"). Therefore, Seasons One through Three of ***Star Wars: The Mandalorian*** must all be set in 9 ABY as well. 17. ↑ [17.0](#cite_ref-Hollywood_Reporter_17-0) [17.1](#cite_ref-Hollywood_Reporter_17-1) [17.2](#cite_ref-Hollywood_Reporter_17-2) [Premium-Era-real](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/0e/Premium-Era-real.png/revision/latest?cb=20241019125517) [Jon Favreau Unveils 'Star Wars' Series 'The Mandalorian,' Marvel Plans and a New Venture](https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/news/jon-favreau-unveils-star-wars-series-mandalorian-marvel-plans-a-new-venture-1233239) by Belloni, Matthew on [*The Hollywood Reporter*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter "wikipedia:The Hollywood Reporter") ([August 21](/wiki/August_21 "August 21"), [2019](/wiki/2019 "2019")) ([backup link](https://web.archive.org/web/20200427021901/https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/news/jon-favreau-unveils-star-wars-series-mandalorian-marvel-plans-a-new-venture-1233239) archived on [April 27](/wiki/April_27 "April 27"), [2020](/wiki/2020 "2020")) 18. ↑ [18.0](#cite_ref-Unmasked_18-0) [18.1](#cite_ref-Unmasked_18-1) [18.2](#cite_ref-Unmasked_18-2) [Premium-Era-real](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/0e/Premium-Era-real.png/revision/latest?cb=20241019125517) [*The Mandalorian* unmasked: 'We did things no Star Wars fan has ever seen'](https://ew.com/tv/2019/09/05/inside-the-mandalorian-star-wars) by Hibberd, James on [*Entertainment Weekly*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly "wikipedia:Entertainment Weekly") ([September 5](/wiki/September_5 "September 5"), [2019](/wiki/2019 "2019")) ([backup link](https://web.archive.org/web/20200422184403/https://ew.com/tv/2019/09/05/inside-the-mandalorian-star-wars) archived on [April 22](/wiki/April_22 "April 22"), [2020](/wiki/2020 "2020")) 19.
